As a result of the election, Chen Runsheng and eight others were elected as directors, Zhang Jinfu and five others were elected as alternate directors, and Han Shilin and five others were elected as supervisors, and Li Zhaomin and three others were elected as alternate supervisors.

The County Government Sends Personnel to Re-examine the House Tax

In order to reorganize the house tax in urban and rural areas, the Wujin County Government has organized a review committee, which decided to reorganize the house tax in urban and rural areas in accordance with the investigation register of the Public Security Bureau. The collection of housing tax has been temporarily suspended. The county government sent personnel yesterday to carry the old register and the investigation register to various districts to re-examine the house tax in conjunction with the Public Security Branch and the District Office. After the re-examination is completed, the house tax will be levied accordingly.

Yangzhou 91

Prevention and Control of Rice Stem Borer in the Third and Fifth Districts

Previously, rice stem borer outbreaks occurred in the third and fifth districts of Jiangdu. Irrigation methods were used to eliminate the pests, and fortunately, a major disaster was averted. Now, Jian Ying has dispatched personnel to collaborate with Jin Yiru, the director of the agricultural extension division, to conduct an on-site investigation. They believe that the root of the rice stem borer has not been completely eradicated and that there is a possibility of future outbreaks. On the 28th, the county government, in order to be cautious, specially invited representatives from the second item of the provincial regulations for the rice stem borer control campaign outline and convened the county party headquarters, extension division, public education center, sericulture improvement district, public security bureau, and district chiefs to form a propaganda committee to implement prevention and control measures. A meeting was scheduled for 2:00 PM on March 7th at the county government to discuss the measures.

Business Tax Bureau to be Reclassified as Second Class

During this spring's Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce meeting in Yangzhou, the Jiangdu County Chamber of Commerce reported on the state of commercial decline and requested that the provincial government be informed and that a branch of the Farmers' Bank of China be established in Yangzhou and the business tax rate be reduced to provide relief. It has recently come to light that the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce has received a provincial government order regarding the request to establish a Farmers' Bank branch, stating that it has been ordered to be reviewed by the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers' Bank Supervisory Committee. As for the reduction of the business tax rate, it is said that the Finance Department is well aware of the economic difficulties in Yangzhou and will approve the reclassification of the business tax bureau as a second-class bureau, with an annual tax of 75,000 yuan. Jiangdu was originally a first-class bureau with an annual tax of 125,000 yuan. This time, the Finance Department's ability to reduce the tax burden in this way, showing compassion for the hardships of businesses, should be welcomed by the general business community.

Gaoyou 92

Two Robberies in the Second District

In the fourth bao of Ruilin Township, Second District of this county, the home of Deng Zaishan, a resident, was suddenly invaded by more than ten robbers, each carrying guns and sharp blades, at about 1:00 AM the other night. They broke into the house and conducted a thorough search, resulting in the loss of over 200 yuan worth of clothing and other items. Additionally, in the 20th bao, 14th jia, 11th household of Jingou Township in the same district, the home of Wang Baogang, a resident with a modest livelihood, was suddenly invaded by seven or eight bandits, each carrying guns. They broke into the house, tied up the family members with ropes, and then looted the entire place, resulting in significant losses. After the two families were robbed, they separately reported the incidents to the county government and requested that the robbers be apprehended and brought to justice.

Liuhe 93

County Government Plans to Develop Park

The county government and local figures previously planned to develop a local park, but the project was halted due to the large amount of funding required. It has now been heard that County Magistrate Qi is planning to develop a park. The construction costs are estimated at over 2,000 yuan, which will be allocated from the construction expenses. The plan has been submitted to the provincial government for approval, and construction will begin once approval is obtained.

County Government Requests Further Allocation of Arrears

Due to poor harvests in the past, the county's education funds have been in arrears for more than five months, resulting in teachers' salaries being delayed. Subsequently, the Department of Education instructed that all arrears owed to dismissed and voluntarily retired teachers should be paid from the surplus funds of the 22nd fiscal year. The county government has stated that the surplus funds have been exhausted by the end of the first semester of the 24th fiscal year, and the teachers' arrears have not yet been fully cleared. Continued payments are still required. They have now submitted another document to the Department of Education requesting permission to allocate surplus funds from the 23rd fiscal year for payment.

Bengbu 94

Police District Consolidation Completed

In order to reduce police expenses, the Public Security Bureau consolidated the five districts into three. The newly appointed head of the First Branch Bureau, Ming Chao Yu, and the head of the Third Branch Bureau, Yang Yin, took office yesterday. The First and Third Branch Bureaus have been consolidated, and the First Branch Bureau has laid off more than ten old and weak police officers. The Second and Fourth Branch Bureaus have been consolidated. The Fourth Branch Bureau has been taken over by personnel sent by Xu Shuzhong, the head of the Second Branch Bureau. A small number of police officers who were left over have been relocated. The old sites of the Third and Fourth Branch Bureaus have been converted into substations. The Fifth Branch Bureau has been renamed the Third Branch Bureau and continues to operate as usual. Each of the three branch bureaus has added one bureau staff member. The police force has been streamlined, with the weaker officers being laid off and the stronger officers being retained. The number of posts has not been reduced, but there have been some changes in the police officers on duty. On the 28th, Director-General He Guoliang, accompanied by Inspector Cao Jizheng, personally went to each branch bureau to call the roll and give instructions. It is heard that the two squadrons originally under the jurisdiction of the Security Brigade will be reduced to one squadron. The title of "Brigade" will be abolished, and the current Brigade Commander Lu Taikun will remain as the squadron leader. The two squadron leaders will be transferred to new positions, which will be announced in the coming days.

Mongolia in the Scramble between Japan and Russia 95

—Translated from A. Grabowsky of Hungary by Bu Ren

Manchuria, which is extremely important in itself, is also a first-class strategic base: this significance is becoming increasingly clear. Manchuria's gateway, the historic road between the mountains and the coast, leads to North China. The Liaodong Peninsula faces Confucius's hometown, the wealthy Shandong Province, across the sea.

Mongolia borders Manchuria. Therefore, the Manchurian problem has raised the Mongolian problem. In recent months, the Japanese have been very active in Mongolia. "Disputes" occur constantly. On the Soviet side, there has been a corresponding reaction. Originally, the Soviet Union regarded Outer Mongolia as its territory and Inner Mongolia as its sphere of influence. According to Moscow dispatches, the Red Army's 16th elite unit is heading to Chita, where it will be stationed, ready to enter the Mongolian border at any time. The demands of "Manchukuo" on Outer Mongolia and Japan's efforts to separate Outer Mongolia from the Soviet sphere of influence have caused deep concern in Moscow's diplomatic circles. The third competitor in this area is China. In 1923, the Soviet Union clearly stated that Outer Mongolia should be an integral part of the Republic of China. Currently, China is no longer mentioned.

It is well known that Outer Mongolia and Inner Mongolia are different. However, in addition to Outer Mongolia and Inner Mongolia, we can also see a third or even fourth part of Mongolia. The third part is the Soviet state known as Tannu Uriankhai. In September 1921, Russia recognized the independence of Tannu Uriankhai, but in fact it is an important part of the Soviet Union. The entire population of Tannu Uriankhai is only 60,000, and its capital, Khem-Beldyr, is said to have a population of 1,000. Tannu Uriankhai became independent, or rather, Russian-owned, in 1921.

Russia's close relationship with Outer Mongolia began before the Great War. This was the result of the Anglo-Russian Entente of 1907. The Anglo-Russian Entente divided the spheres of influence of the two countries in Asia, assigning Outer Mongolia to Russia. From then on, Outer Mongolia and Tannu Uriankhai tended to merge with Siberia. Tannu Uriankhai is the upper reaches of the Yenisey River, surrounded by the Sayan Mountains and the Tannu-Ola Mountains, and isolated from the rest of Mongolia.

On the other hand, the upper reaches of the Selenga River, which flows into Lake Baikal, and the sources of several major streams of the Heilong River are contained within Outer Mongolia.

Speaking of the Heilong River, one cannot avoid raising the issue of Manchuria again. During the period when Russia was developing its power in Manchuria, especially northern Manchuria, it was impossible for Japan to invade Mongolia. However, currently, Manchuria is virtually subordinate to Japan, and this close relationship is effective. Inner Mongolia is immediately threatened because most of Inner Mongolia, namely the Gobi Plateau, slopes toward Manchuria. The Greater Khingan Range, which is generally regarded as a barrier, is actually just a range of hills with a few high peaks. The occupation of Inner Mongolia by Manchuria predates the Manchurian conquest of China. After the Qing Dynasty gained power in China, the relationship between the Manchurian government and the Inner Mongolian government became even closer. At that time, even Outer Mongolia was included in the Manchurian sphere of influence.

From then on, the main route was from the Chinese capital, Beijing, through the Gobi Desert, to Kulun, and then through Kyakhta to Lake Baikal and Irkutsk. This was the famous trade route. At one time, this was the only route for tea merchants to Europe. Currently, there is a railway between Beijing and Zhangjiakou, and a motor road from Zhangjiakou onwards. However, the road was much busier in the Zamaan era when the caravans were flourishing than it is today. The endless caravans on that historic route have long since disappeared. All this traffic has been replaced by cheap ocean shipping. This change has diminished the world's attention to Mongolia, and Mongolia has gradually shifted from Chinese hands to Russian hands without anyone noticing.

During the Great War, Mongolia attracted attention again. In the so-called "Twenty-One Demands," Japan demanded special rights in eastern Mongolia. At that time, Japan was still an ally of Russia; therefore, it was careful not to mention the entire territory of Mongolia, but only the part adjacent to Manchuria. However, the cession of the entire Mongolia was what Japan really desired.

After the Russian Revolution, Japan immediately took action. Its first step was to gain a foothold in Siberia, and its second step was to collaborate with the White Russians in Mongolia to support Baron Ungern-Sternberg in a move to secede from both China and Russia. Baron Ungern-Sternberg eventually failed, was captured by the Red Russians, and was sentenced to death by firing squad in October 1921. Japan was forced to gradually abandon Siberia due to the united resistance of Britain and Russia. On October 25, 1920, it abandoned its last base, Vladivostok. Nevertheless, Japan's ambitions were not dead; it was waiting for the second opportunity to arrive. During the era of cooperation between Red Russia and "pink China," Japan drew up a counter-offensive plan. It planned to start from Outer Mongolia and deliver a fatal blow to Siberia and the Siberian Railway, cutting off Russia's vital lifeline.

Japan's desire for Outer Mongolia has been intensified by the construction and planning of Soviet railways. The Turkestan-Siberia Railway built by the Soviet Union, connecting Turkestan and Siberia, is closely connected with China in the Almaty area and is awaiting a branch line within China. Until now, China has only one trunk line, starting from Beijing and passing through Hankou to reach Guangzhou, and even the section from Hankou to Guangzhou has not been fully completed. In addition to this straight railway, sooner or later a lateral railway will be added, passing through the old gateway of Dzungaria and reaching the upper reaches of the Yellow River, connecting with the Pinghan Railway line. The lateral route will start from Almaty, and from then on, Almaty will become a traffic city of world importance. After the road is built, it will allow travelers passing through the mainland to China to avoid the roundabout route via Harbin and Fengtian; they can pass through Baku, the Caspian Sea, Turkestan or Central Siberia, directly to the interior of China. Such Sino-Russian contact is bound to have serious consequences. Namely: the Manchurian Railway owned by Japan will be ignored.

The occupation of Outer Mongolia allows the Soviet Union to control the gateway to Dzungaria—the fourth part of Mongolia. The Soviet Union is also planning to build another railway, passing through Outer Mongolia along that historic trade route. On September 20, 1925, the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia signed a contract: the Soviet Union has the right to build a railway from Chita to Kulun, and stipulated that a 66-mile wide zone on each side of the railway as a railway area. Of course, this route will later be extended to Zhangjiakou.

It is necessary to clarify a common misconception about the Gobi Desert. The Gobi is not purely barren, nor is it the true desert indicated by the word "desert." Especially the eastern Gobi, blessed by monsoon rains, has a number of grasslands, which are excellent pastures. For this reason, Outer Mongolia may extend its borders into Inner Mongolia deep into the Gobi. The social institutions of Outer Mongolia are changing drastically. The Lama system is about to disappear there, so the population is expanding very rapidly. This result will necessitate the expansion of its territory.

The future development of Mongolia is far beyond what most people can imagine. It has a lot of natural resources. Its strategic and geographical position is very important. Currently, its international situation is changing.

China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) Dispatches Plane Yesterday to Supply Foreign Merchant Ships off Dagu Port, Carrying Food Back and Forth Between Tianjin and Dagu Four Times, Dropping Over Three Thousand Pounds of Beef and Bread 96

China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) dispatched a plane yesterday to rescue foreign merchant ships trapped by ice off Dagu Port, dropping a total of over three thousand pounds of bread and beef. The reporter from the China Eastern News Agency wrote the following special report yesterday:

Stranded for Over a Month, Food Supplies Depleted

Due to the severe cold in North China, the Hai River off Dagu Port has frozen over, reaching a thickness of dozens of feet, unprecedented in recent years. This has resulted in dozens of merchant ships being trapped in the ice on the sea surface for over a month. All fuel and food supplies have been depleted.

CNAC Dispatches Plane for Rescue

As the situation was critical, merchants in Tianjin requested the Tianjin Maritime Administration to consult with CNAC to dispatch a plane for rescue. Considering it had an inescapable duty, the company immediately agreed, ordering the Douglas aircraft flying the Shanghai-Pingnan route from Ping to Shanghai yesterday to provide assistance while flying over Tianjin and Dagu.

Dropping Meat and Noodles, Reaching Three Thousand Pounds

After departing from Ping at around 7:00 AM yesterday, the aircraft arrived in Tianjin at 8:00 AM. First, it loaded 600 pounds of beef and noodles in Tianjin and flew to Dagu Port to drop them at the locations where the ships were trapped. Upon returning to Tianjin, a CNAC spokesperson told the China Eastern News Agency reporter yesterday that the aircraft made a total of four round trips between Tianjin and Dagu yesterday, dropping approximately 3,000 pounds of food items, including half-meat noodles.

Shanghai Bank Promotes Acceptance Bills, Acceptance Period Limited to 120 Days, Discount Rate Set by the Bank from Time to Time 98

In order to assist industrial and commercial enterprises, the Shanghai Bank is promoting the discounting and acceptance of acceptance bills. It has announced its articles of association and explanations, with the acceptance period limited to 120 days and the discount rate set from time to time. The details are as follows, as handled by the Ministry of Commerce.

Articles of Association for Acceptance Discount of Bills

Article 1: The bank will handle the acceptance and discounting of bills in order to serve society and assist industrial and commercial enterprises. Article 2: Companies and firms that have been issued advance payment letters of credit by the bank or have entered into an acceptance contract with the bank may issue bills payable by the bank within the specified scope and have them accepted by the bank. Article 3: The acceptance handling fee will be determined and charged by the bank according to the face value of the bill. Article 4: The term of a bill accepted by the bank shall be limited to 120 days. Article 5: Any bank acceptance bill or commercial acceptance bill that has been recognized by the bank may be discounted. Article 6: Commercial acceptance bills shall be limited to those arising from genuine goods transactions. Article 7: The discount rate may be determined by the bank at any time. Article 8: If a bill discounted by the bank is not paid upon maturity, the issuer, endorser, acceptor, and guarantor shall be jointly and severally liable. Article 9: The bank may amend these articles of association at any time.

Meaning and Types of Acceptance Bills

Chapter 1: Meaning of Acceptance Bills. Goods transactions can be divided into cash payment, credit account, promissory notes, and bills of exchange. Cash payment and credit account are the most common methods. A promissory note, also known as a term note, is issued by the buyer to the seller to pay by the due date. As for a bill of exchange, it is issued by the seller, requesting the buyer to pay on a certain date. After the buyer acknowledges the bill, he signs it, which is called "acceptance" in the law of negotiable instruments, and is called an acceptance bill. Chapter 2: Types and Generation Methods of Acceptance Bills. Acceptance bills are divided into commercial acceptance bills and bank acceptance bills. (A) "Commercial": Commercial documentary acceptance bills occur in inter-city goods trade, where the seller exports and advances payment, and the buyer entrusts the purchase certificate. Commercial non-documentary acceptance bills occur in local goods trade. (B) "Bank": Occur in inter-city goods trade, where the seller enters into an acceptance contract, and the buyer requests to open an advance payment letter of credit. Occur in local goods, where mortgaged industrial and commercial enterprises enter into an acceptance contract.

Functions Can Revitalize the Market

Chapter 3: Functions of Acceptance Bills. The credit account system has been affected by the contraction of silver outflow, and should be abolished, and replaced by acceptance bills, so that industrial and commercial enterprises can operate on their own, and the market can increase its bargaining chips. It is similar in nature to expanding currency, but without the disadvantages of expanding currency. (A) For the seller: It can make capital turnover more flexible, expand the scope of business, reduce bad debt losses, reduce collection staff, reduce the cost of goods, and clarify internal accounts. (B) For the buyer: It can reduce the cost of goods, make capital turnover more flexible, increase their own credit, and expand the scope of business. (C) For the financial market: It can make capital turnover methods flexible and safe, and the market stable, and can create a situation of controlling the market and reducing interest rates.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry of Finance to Request Exemption from Stamp Tax on Acceptance Bills 99

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting exemption from stamp tax on commercial acceptance bills. To the Honorable Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, all industries in this city, in view of the economic decline and financial exhaustion, in order to improve the credit account system and activate capital, initiated the implementation of acceptance bills last year to provide relief. However, the matter is still in its initial stage and needs to be promoted. This acceptance bill is a basis for both the seller and the buyer to agree on a payment date in a transaction, which is different from the use of ordinary bills of exchange. Moreover, it is a newly tried negotiable instrument, and it will not damage the original source of stamp tax. As for its circulation in the market and assistance to the economy, it is more effective than the temporarily exempted checks. The Committee for Promoting Acceptance Bills of the affiliated association proposed to petition the government for commercial acceptance bills to be temporarily exempted from stamp duty, following the example of checks, in order to encourage them. It is proposed that the Honorable Ministry examine and approve the petition, and then submit it to the Executive Yuan, stating that it is necessary to encourage the circulation of the acceptance bills, and requesting it to consult the Legislative Yuan to exempt them from stamp duty, following the example of checks, which is a matter of public convenience. Sincerely, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

National Federation of Commerce Cables the Central Government to Change the Silver Management Rules to Avoid Restrictions on the Silver Content to Maintain the Livelihoods of Hundreds of Thousands of Silversmiths 104

Shiye She (Industry News) reported that the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce telegraphed the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating, "Recently, we received a report from the representatives of the national silversmith industry, Ran Xizhang, Fu Shengmao, Cai Jilun, Gu Suming, Zou Jizhi, Xiao Junjian, Xia Zuomin, Xu Guangde, Li Gengnian, Zhan Yufu, Ge Yuanchang, Lu Junqing, Zhang Boxun, Han Jiuhua, Huang Haibo, Wu Junsan, Yu Wenkang, etc., stating, 'Since we received the silver management rules for silver products promulgated by the Ministry of Finance in November last year, limiting the use of chemical silver to 30% when necessary, we have been frightened and do not know what to do. It is generally believed that chemical silver is beneficial for machine manufacturing and cannot be competed with by handcrafts. Even if 30% of pure silver is added, it is still hard and brittle, and cannot withstand hammering. Silversmiths in various provinces have requested the Ministry of Finance to revise the rules and exempt the restrictions on the silver content. However, the Ministry of Finance has repeatedly rejected the requests, stating that there is no need to discuss them and has not allowed any changes. The decrees are majestic, and small merchants dare not have any other opinions. However, considering the livelihoods of silversmiths across the country, it is really difficult to bow our heads and wait for death, and it is also closely related to national culture and customs. We dare to risk offense and appeal to your association to clarify the situation. Chemical silver is hard and brittle, which is well known to the Ministry of Finance, so its instructions state, "But if it is heated and hammered, it will not feel difficult." However, even if it can barely be made into a vessel, it must be heated and hammered, and it cannot be exquisite and beautiful, and will eventually be abandoned by society. This company has always used pure silver to manufacture jewelry, but for utensils, 88 silver is used. However, it is already difficult to work with. The reason for doing so is to make the material slightly stronger, not easy to be dented, and to resist imported silver products. It is not something we enjoy doing. Now, if we are forced to use chemical silver and restrict the silver content, then it will be difficult for silversmiths to apply their skills. I am afraid that foreigners who use machines will take this opportunity to compete with machine-made products, flocking here to take away our thousands of years of craftsmanship and cause silversmiths across the country to be eliminated. I hope you will consider that the original intention of this prohibition on silver products is only to prevent the outflow of silver. However, there is no need to worry about the outflow of silver products. Those who dare to defy the law and smuggle goods are only seeking profit. This company never sells unfinished silver materials. The silver utensils and silver ornaments sold must be charged with wages in addition to the value of the silver materials, or even more than the original silver price. How can smugglers profit from this? If you worry that some unscrupulous people in the same industry may secretly sell unfinished silver materials and cause leakage, then the same industry can provide joint guarantees, and the customs can strictly prohibit smuggling, which is enough to choke off smuggling. Why give up eating because of choking, and cut off the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people? The operating difficulties of the same industry in recent years are like frost-covered yellow leaves that fall without shaking. Whether they survive or die, they are left to nature. Now, the government not only does not cultivate them but cuts them down. If these hundreds of thousands of workers become unemployed, I do not know how the government will deal with them. Therefore, we are forced to appeal to you in addition to submitting a petition, asking your association to investigate the facts, grant us assistance, and submit a request to revise the silver management rules to exempt the restrictions on the silver content so that handicrafts can be manufactured to maintain the livelihoods of silversmiths across the country and implement Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Principle of People's Livelihood. We submit this urgent appeal with the utmost gratitude." Accordingly, we should telegraph your government to review this matter. We earnestly request that you consider the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of silversmiths and approve the change of the silver management rules. This matter is extremely urgent. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, respectfully kowtows. Winter Seal.

Page 10

Taxpayers Association Asks the Municipal Council to Stop the Electricity Company's Reckless Actions. Suddenly Claiming Damage Two Days After Replacing a Meter. Craftsmen Not Verified, Users Not Responsible for Hard Records. 105

Xin Sheng She (New Voice News) reports that the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Secretary-General of the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir, recently, we received a letter from the Tiechunji Barber Shop at 796 Huade Road, stating that the merchant has been operating the Tiechunji Barber Shop at 796 Huade Road in the Public Concession. On July 2, 1930, they installed an electricity meter from the Shanghai Electricity Company and have been using electric lights for more than five years. On February 17 this year, several workers from the Electricity Company suddenly came to the shop, removed the old meter, and replaced it with a new meter, saying that the code had run out and needed to be replaced, etc. Unexpectedly, after removing the meter, on February 19, they received a letter in English from the Electricity Company, stating that the old meter had been damaged by the shop, each hundred characters must be slowed by sixteen characters, calculated for more than five years, the loss should be 193 yuan, 6 jiao, and 9 fen, and they were ordered to pay it off within 48 hours, or else the power would be cut off, etc. The merchant went to the Electricity Company on Feilun Road and repeatedly pleaded, but there was no room for recovery, and they only agreed to pay in four installments. They had no choice but to raise 50 yuan and go to the Electricity Company in Tilanqiao on February 20 to pay it, on the one hand, to extend the period and prepare a letter to your association, advocating justice and sending someone to verify the truth. The merchant has not damaged anything and cannot bear this unreasonable oppression. We ask you to negotiate according to reason and help the merchant out of the trap." The association checked that the installation of electricity meters for electric light users is strictly controlled by the company, and the sealing is strict to prevent users from stealing electricity. Now, according to the barber shop, the Shanghai Electricity Company removed the old meter and installed a new meter on February 17, and on the 19th of the same month, the company sent a written statement, saying that the old meter was damaged, each hundred characters must be slowed by sixteen percent, and the loss must be calculated from the year the meter was installed, and the barber shop was limited to paying it off within 48 hours. Regarding the so-called loss fee of the company, there are two points that we must ask your bureau to instruct the company to pay attention to. 1. When the craftsman removed the meter, they should have first verified the hard record on the meter. At that time, the craftsman who removed the meter did not declare that the meter's hard record was damaged. 2. It was not until two days after the old meter was taken away that it was said to be damaged. It should be known that the hard record on the meter is intact, and the user is not responsible for other internal damage and slow-running responsibility. Moreover, the meter has been installed for more than five years, and the company is responsible for compensating for the electricity fee that has been running slowly for more than five years, which further proves that the meter was undoubtedly damaged when it was installed five years ago. According to the above, we should write to your bureau and quickly stop the company from acting rashly. All losses suffered by the store should be compensated by it. We address this to the Secretary-General of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council."

The Captain of the Ruikang Ship Barely Escapes From Dagu to Shanghai. Reports That Various Ships Are Trapped, and the Situation Is Terrible. No Good Solution for Relief, Shipping Companies Lose More Than Ten Million. 108

Shen Shi She (Shanghai Times) reports that the commercial ships trapped outside Dagu Port for more than two months due to ice is an unprecedentedly serious situation in decades. Shipping companies have suffered huge losses, and there is no way to provide relief. Although food has been distributed by plane recently, it is a drop in the bucket and still does not help. Mr. So-and-so, the captain of the Ruikang ship of the Shou Kang Shipping Company in this port, recently escaped and came to Shanghai. According to his report, the situation is extremely miserable. The details are as follows:

Escaping to Shanghai

According to the report of Mr. So-and-so, the captain of the Ruikang ship, the Ruikang ship has been trapped in Dagu Port by ice for more than a month. He happened to encounter a favorable wind and current a month ago, which blew away the ice surrounding the ship, so he was able to find a way to leave the ship and come to Shanghai to report to the company and ask for assistance as soon as possible. The ships have been stuck on the ice for a long time, and the situation is quite miserable. There is a lack of food and fuel. He also went without food for a week, so his body has not yet recovered. The situation of other ships can also be seen from this. Moreover, the losses are in the millions.

Losses of Tens of Millions

According to news from shipping circles, the Tianjin Navigation Administration has been trying to provide relief since the ships were trapped. However, because the ice is very solid, the icebreaker ships have lost their effectiveness. As for the distribution of food by plane, most of it is lost because it is thrown from the sky. Only half of what is thrown can reach the trapped ships, which may not be enough to satisfy the majority of people. But other than this, there is no other good solution. As for the shipping industry, it is also at a loss and unable to provide assistance. It is estimated that the losses of shipping companies will exceed tens of millions. It is still difficult to predict when the situation will improve.

Central Savings Society to Open Soon; Civil Servant Savings Regulations to Be Promulgated; Managed by the Savings Department of the Central Trust Bureau 117

The Central Savings Society is approved to open before the end of the month, handling prize-linked savings and civil servant savings, managed by the Savings Department of the Central Trust Bureau. Details are recorded as follows:

Prize-Linked Savings Registration

The Central Trust Bureau allocated a capital of RMB 5 million to establish the Central Savings Society to handle prize-linked savings. After the Bureau took over the former Sino-French Savings Bank's prize-linked savings, registration, although it had been cut off in the north, was continued to accommodate depositors in remote provinces. It is now nearing completion. As all preparations are in place, it is approved to open before the end of this month. The exact opening date is being discussed by Manager Li Shuming and Director Ye Zhuotang. After opening, in addition to handling the Central Prize-Linked Savings, it will also handle the prize-linked savings of the Savings Department of the China Industrial Bank.

Civil Servant Savings Law

Civil Servant Savings Decided to Be Managed by Central Trust Bureau

Civil servant savings will be managed by the Savings Department of the Central Trust Bureau. The regulations have been approved by the Central Political Conference and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. They will be implemented after promulgation by the National Government. The regulations consist of 15 articles, stipulating that each agency will deduct a certain amount from the monthly salary of each civil servant and deposit it with the Central Trust Bureau. The civil servant can withdraw the savings upon retirement or death. The Central Trust Bureau will determine the most favorable interest rate based on financial conditions and calculate it using compound interest. A reserve fund will be allocated and managed independently.

Retrial of Zhang Xuebin Case Scheduled for Pronouncement; Result: Continued Hearing on the Morning of the 9th 124

Zhang Xuebin, a martial artist who claims to be the authentic successor of the Lingji sect of the Shaolin Temple in Sichuan, was introduced by Shen Huating, who resided at 13 Xinminli, Beierbu Road, in August of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. He entered into a contract with Dahuhua Garden on Haige Road to set up a plum blossom stake platform to compete in martial arts. Shen Huating and Sun Lie acted as guarantors. On October 7th of that year, Zhang Xuebin performed on stage but greatly disappointed the audience. As a result, Feng Yixiang, the manager of Dahuhua Garden, demanded compensation for various losses from Zhang, Shen, and Sun, but to no avail. In January of this year, Feng filed a complaint with the civil division of the Special Second Court, suing the three for compensation of RMB 11,097 in actual losses and repayment of a loan of RMB 1,900. As the defendants could not be reached, the case was concluded after unilateral pleading after public notice was served. Recently, Shen Huating filed a motion stating that he still resided in Shanghai and wished to appear in court to defend himself. Yesterday morning, Judge Ma Shuyi presided over a new hearing in court seven. Defendant Shen Huating appeared in court with his lawyer. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the grounds for the lawsuit and the objects of the request for judgment and presented the contract, the loan receipt, and the bill for various losses. Defendant Shen Huating acknowledged the contract and the loan receipt and defended the claim for damages, stating that the issue of liability must be resolved first. Zhang Xuebin did have skills and had demonstrated them to the plaintiff before the opening. He said that a month of practice was needed to perform for the public. However, Chinese martial artists have always been jealous, and they sabotaged the performance. Zhang Xuebin declared before the competition that he wanted to compete on the stage, but they insisted that Zhang compete off the stage, which was of course impossible. They then considered Zhang to be unskilled and stopped his performance on the second day because Dahuhua Garden did not publish advertisements. Judge Ma then asked the plaintiff's lawyer if anyone had gone on stage to compete with Zhang Xuebin. The plaintiff's lawyer replied that there were martial artists, young and old, from far and wide, who, upon seeing Zhang Xuebin's actions, laughed at him for being a charlatan and swindler, and no one would fight him on the ring. Then, the lawyer was asked about the bill, so he ordered the hearing to be continued on the morning of March 9.

Three Convicts in Private Sale of Counterfeit Coins Scheduled for Pronouncement; Yao Xiaobing and Others Ordered to Be Detained 125

Yao Xiaobing, a native of Changshu, was suspected of privately selling counterfeit one-yuan coins of the Bank of China. Ma Zhongrong, a Chinese detective of the New Gate Police Station, and detective Xu Zhengting found out about it. They encountered Yao on Chongqing Road and Dagu Road the day before yesterday, posing as customers and asking Yao to buy the counterfeit coins. At the time, it was stated that 100 counterfeit coins would be sold for 26 yuan. The detectives first paid 13 yuan and handed it to Yao, who took the money and left. Shortly after, Yao brought 50 one-yuan counterfeit coins and was arrested by the detectives and taken to the police station. Subsequently, based on his confession, they went to 120 Annajin Road and 18 Jinxiufang, Geluk Road, with detectives from the French Police Station and apprehended two accomplices, Yang Guisheng and Zhu Fusheng. They also seized 35 similar counterfeit coins at Zhu's house and took them all back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, in accordance with Article 196 of the Criminal Law, the three were transferred to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court for public prosecution on charges of counterfeiting and circulating currency. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, stated the facts of the case and submitted the counterfeit notes. Defendant Yang Guisheng confessed that he had opened the Republican Teahouse at 453 Miti Neiyin Road in the French Concession. On January 10 of this year, he learned that someone was privately manufacturing these counterfeit coins, so he reported to the Western detectives of the French Police Station. The detectives arrested a number of suspects and seized a large number of counterfeit coins. He then picked up 100 of the counterfeit coins and took them back to the teahouse. One day, he showed them to the public and was seen by Yao Xiaobing and Zhu Fusheng. Zhu was a carpenter foreman who often came to his teahouse for tea, so he knew him. The day before yesterday, Zhu came to his teahouse to take the counterfeit notes, saying that he could take them to the countryside for gambling. He gave them all to Zhu because he thought they were useless to keep, totaling 85. The remaining 15 were discarded by his children. Later, Zhu handed over 11 yuan, which he received. Zhu Fusheng confessed that Yao Xiaobing had the idea of selling the counterfeit notes and asked him to fetch them from Yang Guisheng's place. At the time, Yao handed him 11 yuan to give to Yang, etc. When questioned, Yao Xiaobing confessed that he received 13 yuan from the detectives and handed 11 yuan to Zhu without denying it. Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the confessions and ordered the three defendants to be detained and await sentencing on Wednesday of this week.

Chinese detectives from the Public Concession Police Station arrested Wei Haichen, a person using counterfeit nickel coins, on Xiaoshadu Road a few days ago. Under the assets of the company, there are 50 old automobiles, which should be auctioned by the bankruptcy administrator in conjunction with the supervisors, with the highest bidder winning.

Judgment in the Iron Blood Love Silk Lawsuit Written by Zhang Henshui 131

Huadong News Agency reports that the small local newspaper Jin Gang Tie Bao published the martial arts novel "Iron Blood Love Silk" by the famous novelist Zhang Henshui in the 21st year of the Republic of China. Cui Dingming, the owner of Samsung Bookstore, learned about this and asked Shi Jiqun, the manager of the newspaper, to negotiate and voluntarily sign a contract to wholesale the book. Shi also expressed his willingness. Therefore, the contract was signed on December 1, 22nd year of the Republic of China. The contract stipulated that at least 2,000 copies should be wholesaled each year. Unexpectedly, after the contract was signed, 900 yuan was owed for the books, and Cui did not fulfill many of the terms stipulated in the contract. Furthermore, Cui's business failed, and after the bookstore closed, he disappeared without a trace. Shi was bound by the contract and has not been able to reprint the book until now. He then hired lawyer Jiang Zongpan to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court. Judge Cao Jun granted the public service. After several hearings, the verdict was pronounced the other day. The defendant, Cui Dingming, should clear the book payment of 900 yuan, and the contract between the two parties was allowed to be terminated. The litigation fee was borne by the defendant. It is heard that after Shi received the verdict, he re-printed the book "Iron Blood Love Silk" because Zhang Henshui's novels have always been popular with the public and is preparing to distribute it directly to meet the needs of readers.

Neighboring Garden Fire: Yao Guixiang Dies of Shock-Induced Illness 133

A local man named Yao Guixiang, 38 years old, residing at No. [無號] in Lane 319, Zhoushan Road, used to be a blacksmith. His residence was next to the private garden of Gan Chixian, a compradore at the Gonghexiang Wharf. The garden owner, fearing that the recent cold weather would hinder the growth of his plants, had installed hotbeds to ward off the cold. On the afternoon of the previous day, the hotbeds suddenly caught fire, with fierce smoke billowing out. Yao, noticing this from outside the garden, quickly reported the fire. Subsequently, the Huishan Patrol Station dispatched Chinese detective Zhao Yongqing and others, along with the fire brigade, who arrived in vehicles to extinguish the fire. The fire was soon put out. During the firefighting efforts, Yao also followed the detectives into the garden near the fire's origin to observe. Unexpectedly, fearing that the fire would spread to his own house, Yao became extremely frightened. While conversing with the detectives, he suddenly collapsed and lost consciousness. The detectives summoned an ambulance, which rushed him to Tongren Hospital, but to no avail. He died shortly after. His body was transported to the Philan Road morgue for examination. Yesterday morning, Zhang Zongru, a prosecutor from the First Special Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. According to the statement of Western patrolman Phillips, Prosecutor Zhang determined that the deceased, Yao Guixiang, male, had died from a shock-induced illness. The body was released to his sister-in-law, Yao Aju, after she signed a guarantee for its burial.

Fire in Hongfa Lane, Zhabei: Three Buildings Completely Destroyed; Conflicting Accounts of the Cause 134

At approximately 8:50 PM last night, a fire suddenly broke out at No. 16, Hongfa Lane, Binxing Road West, Qingyun Road, Zhabei, the residence of a Mr. Yin, who works as a broker for an insurance company. At the time, neighboring residents, fearing the fire would spread due to the closely packed houses in the lane, hastily evacuated with their valuables, supporting the elderly and carrying the young. However, the narrow entrance to the lane caused chaos and panic, leaving the fire unattended. Before long, the fire breached the roof and spread to the neighboring buildings at No. 15 and No. 14. Flames soared and lit up the sky. Fortunately, the site was close to the fourth fire brigade of Zhabei, which dispatched fire trucks immediately upon receiving the news. Police officers were also sent by the local police station to maintain order. The order was slightly restored. The firefighters were then able to work to extinguish the fire. It was extinguished around 10:30 PM, but all three buildings had been completely destroyed. Fortunately, there were no injuries, which was considered a great relief amidst the misfortune. The cause of the fire remains unclear, and the police station is currently investigating.

Love Letter Transforms into Death Warrant: Fiancee Commits Suicide in Grief; No Recovery Possible, Life Extinguished; Overseas Lover Unaware of the Calamity 136

Shi Yizhang, a Ningbo native currently residing at No. 3, Zhaoyuan Lane, Beishan Road, is 54 years old this year and recently unemployed. His wife passed away long ago, leaving behind a daughter named Shandi, who is 17 years old this year. Years ago, through a matchmaker, she was betrothed to Zhu Xiaocheng, also from their hometown, who is 30 years old this year. A betrothal gift of 200 yuan was given. Zhu works as a chief steward on a foreign steamship and returns to Shanghai every three to six months. When Shandi was 11 years old, her mother passed away, and her father was away on business, leaving her without care. Moreover, her future in-laws had also passed away. That year, Shandi went to live with her fiance Zhu Xiaocheng's aunt and uncle, surnamed Feng, at No. 20, Puqing Lane, Malang Road, in the French Concession. She has lived there for six years, maintaining a good relationship with her aunt and uncle. Recently, she had been looking forward to Zhu Xiaocheng's return to Shanghai for their wedding. Unexpectedly, out of the blue, Zhu Xiaocheng encountered difficulties making a living overseas and was unable to return to marry. He sent a letter in the form of a poem to his aunt and uncle and his fiancee Shi Shandi, stating that he was too poor to complete the marriage, urging Shandi to marry someone else, and willing to forfeit the previously sent betrothal gift. Upon learning this, Shi Shandi, feeling that she had no face to face the world due to Zhu's rejection, sought to end her life. On the morning of the 29th of last month at 10:00 AM, she went out to buy new shoes and raw opium and returned home. At 8:00 PM that evening, she secretly ingested the raw opium and committed suicide. An hour later, her aunt, Feng Wangshi (45 years old, Ningbo native), discovered her and immediately rushed her to Ximen Obstetrics Hospital at No. 393, Malang Road, for treatment. After resuscitation efforts until 8:00 AM the next morning (the 1st of this month), there was still no sign of recovery. She was then transferred to Renji Hospital, but due to severe poisoning, she could not be saved. At 2:10 PM on the 1st, her life was extinguished. The hospital reported the case to the French Concession police, who dispatched Detective Zhang Chunsheng to investigate the cause of death. The body was transported to Tongren Fuyuantang morgue for examination. Yesterday, Wang Ren, a prosecutor from the Second Special Court, along with forensic doctors and clerks, arrived at the morgue at noon to confirm that Zhu Shi Shandi had died from poisoning. The prosecutor questioned Shi Yizhang, the deceased's father, and Feng Wangshi, the deceased's aunt and uncle. He then ordered that the body be handed over to the deceased's father after signing a guarantee for its burial. Zhu Xiaocheng, the deceased's fiance, is currently overseas and is unaware that his letter of rejection has turned into a death warrant, causing his fiancee to commit suicide in grief. The poem that Zhu sent to the girl and her aunt and uncle is recorded below:

Writing this poem, my heart is filled with tears,

I resent my incompetence, whom else to blame?

Sending this letter to sever ties with my fiancee,

Entrusting her to find another to marry.

The Zhu family's fate is truly bitter,

Our little girl has grown up and is ready to be wed.

The two hundred yuan dowry is nowhere to be found,

These words will enrage the poor and lowly.

I am too old to start a family and make a living,

Shame prevents me from facing my aunt and uncle.

Although the adults may be willing to help,

I fear being ridiculed by others.

This departure will be forever, with little chance of return,

Life and death, survival and demise, are all uncertain.

If we cannot meet in this life,

Perhaps we will be husband and wife in the next.

New Buddhist Organization: World Red "Buddha" Swastika Society; Gathering Monks and Nuns Worldwide to Carry Out Relief and Rescue Work 138

The number of Buddhist monks and nuns in China has not been accurately counted in recent years, but it is estimated to be around four to five hundred thousand. Due to old customs, they lack social organization. Although the Chinese Buddhist Association has been established in recent years, it has not yet been fully organized in terms of rectifying monastic rules. Therefore, it has no time to attend social causes and civilian services. Recently, Venerable Hongming, recognizing the above situation and the imminent global crisis, and adhering to the Buddhist principles of compassion and saving the world, believes that Buddhists should also do their part for humanity. Therefore, he initiated the organization of the "World Red 'Buddha' Swastika Society," equivalent to the Red Cross and Red Swastika Society, to gather the strength of monks and nuns to train in medical rescue work. In peacetime, they will piously recite sutras and pray for peace. Once war breaks out, they will go to the front lines, regardless of friend or foe, to carry out rescue, burial, and assistance to refugees in war zones. Since its inception, Venerable Hongming has been traveling between Beijing and Shanghai and has gained the sympathy of the public. Among the central authorities who have signed their support are Central Committee members Bai Wenwei, Kexing'e, Dai Jitao, Peng Yangguang, Yao Yuping, Yu Youren, Cheng Qian, Zhou Bomin, and others. Prominent figures in society include Wang Yiting, Zhu Ziqiao, Zhao Hengti, Tang Xiangming, Wen Lanting, Zhang Xiaolin, Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, Zhong Kanghou, Yao Minghui, and Zhu Shiseng. Among the monks, Venerable Yuanying, Taixu, Dehao, Hongsan, Dabei, Yingzhao, and Ruisheng are among those who have joined as initiators. Dozens of others, including Xinci, Changxing, Miaoxing, Youlin, and Wansong, have also joined. Currently, Hongming came to Shanghai a few days ago to participate in the public banquet of various charitable organizations honoring Mr. Xu Jingren and is in contact with the Chinese Buddhist Association regarding all matters. He is scheduled to go to Beijing the day after tomorrow to personally meet with Chairman Lin and President Jiang to report everything and then return to Shanghai to convene a meeting to prepare for the organization.

Shanghai County: Extension of Deadline for Clearing Unclaimed Land and Registering Land 145

The Shanghai County Government now announces that the matter of clearing unclaimed private land, supplementing grain, and upgrading the tax classification is crucial for rectifying tax quotas and consolidating property rights for the people. However, the deadline for waiving the supplementary grain fees is approaching, and the number of people reporting and registering is very few. The reason is that land registration is currently being carried out in the county. Those who have land without grain or more land than grain often believe that since they have already registered, they do not need to report and upgrade the tax classification to avoid paying grain taxes at present. If the land and grain do not match, even if they register, they are still privately occupying land without grain until the land tax is collected according to the registered area. For thorough consideration, a report has been submitted to the Finance Department to extend the deadline for waiving the supplementary grain fees to March 15th. Therefore, in addition to making a public announcement, the county government has ordered the district chiefs to urge the township chiefs to explain to the people that those who have land without grain or more land than grain must report and register before March 15th. After the deadline at the end of June, the land will be confiscated if discovered.

The Shanghai Film Industry: Important Statement from the National Salvation Association; Activities Halted Due to Fear of Misunderstandings; Another Chinese Film Industry Association to be Organized 150

The Shanghai Film Industry National Salvation Association issued an important statement yesterday, saying: "Recently, the strong neighbor has been encroaching on North China, and the national crisis is becoming more serious. All sectors of Shanghai have risen up to organize national salvation groups. As citizens of China, we are not to be outdone in loving our country. Therefore, on January 27th of this year, we organized the Shanghai Film Industry National Salvation Association to engage in the national salvation movement. The motive is very simple. However, the allegory issued at the time of establishment included the proposition of 'abolishing the current film censorship system,' which seems to cause suspicion. In fact, our film industry is under the control of foreigners, and patriotic films are often unable to be screened in the concession theaters. The above expression is just a cry of this kind of pain, and there is absolutely no dissatisfaction with the central government's film censorship system. Previously, we saw the Central Propaganda Department's letter to the people of the country, showing the central government's determination to 'seek national self-reliance and self-strengthening internally, and seek national independence and equality externally' to the people of the country. We are deeply moved. However, regarding the establishment of our association, there are many accusations. We ourselves consider that the original intention of organizing the National Salvation Association is no different from the central government's intention. If it causes misunderstandings, it is not what we expected. After discussion, the association has now stopped its activities. The comrades of various companies will organize the Chinese Film Industry Association to follow the central government's intention of serving the country and the people and strive for the revitalization of the Chinese nation under its guidance. This is what we all share."

Reorganization of the Two Roads 154

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus studied the reduction of sections on the two lines, changing the Beijing-Danyang, Danyang-Suzhou, and Suzhou-Songjiang sections of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway into Beijing-Wuxi and Wuxi-Shanghai sections. The Shanghai-Jiaxing, Jiaxing-Zhapu, and Cao-Ningbo sections of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway were changed into Shanghai-Hangzhou and Hangzhou-Ningbo sections. This has been approved, and all engineering, transportation, and mechanical sections will be handled accordingly. It was implemented on March 1. The section chiefs and engineers of each section will remain the original section chiefs and engineers and will be redeployed. The police sections will be determined by the police headquarters upon approval, that is, each of the above four sections will be divided into several sections.

A reporter from the Datong News Agency learned from the inland waterway shipping industry that the Yongshun Steamboat Company and the Yongan Shipping Bureau on North Suzhou Road have merged on the 1st of this month. After the implementation of the merger, both ships have been greatly renovated. In the future, they will travel back and forth every day, it is said.

Rent Reduction Dispute in Yongyu Lane: The Court Rules a 10% Rent Reduction 161

There are more than 170 houses in Yongyu Lane on Ximen Road, Beile Road, French Concession. The tenants, due to the impact of the sluggish market and the high rent, could not afford it. Therefore, last year, they jointly initiated and organized the Yongyu Lane Branch of the Fourth District Sub-Association of the Shanghai Second Special District Citizens' United Association, asking the owner, Shunji Company, to reduce the rent in order to maintain it. Unexpectedly, the owner resolutely refused to oppose the tenants' request. Sun Shengchang, a member of the branch, was sued by the No. 2 Special Court for owing rent and moving out, and a provisional attachment was implemented. Fortunately, the tenant had deposited the rent in the bank and was not seized. Therefore, he immediately hired lawyer Ge Zhitan to file a counterclaim for rent reduction according to law, and all the members participated in the lawsuit. After several trials by the No. 2 Special Court, a judgment was made a few days ago, reducing the rent by 10% from August 24 to July 28. The judgment has been received yesterday. It is learned that the branch has convened a meeting yesterday to discuss, in order to seek fair treatment and to resolve the entire issue, because the original rent of the lane varies, with lane houses ranging from 36 to 50 yuan, and city houses ranging from 24 to 30 yuan. It was resolved to pay the rent in accordance with the rent reduction amount determined by the court, and a letter will be sent to the owner to implement it.

Zili Arts and Crafts Society's New Product: Julijiao Glue: The glue is an essential raw material for industry. The glue used in industry is best animal glue. However, its disadvantage is that it needs to be dissolved in water when used, and it loses its viscosity if the temperature is too high, and it will solidify slightly cold, and it is easy to send off in summer. Shanghai Zili Arts and Crafts Society uses chemical methods and domestic raw materials to produce "Julijiao" glue. The viscosity is greater than ordinary animal glue, and it does not freeze even below the freezing point. It does not rot in summer and has a fragrant smell and clean color. Whether it is wood, stone, glass, bone, horn, ivory, or bakelite, it can be glued. There is no need to boil it when using it, and there is no harm in returning to tide after it is dry and solid. Its properties combine the strengths of Arabic gum. At a time when the price of gum is rising, this glue can be used as a substitute for its products, and it is also a new contribution in the national product voice. Anyone who wants to try it can send a letter to Zili Arts and Crafts Su Society, No. 1 Sida Lane, Shikota Road, Shanghai to take samples.

The Educational Film Association Promotes Instructional Films, Starting with Schools Along the Shanghai-Hangzhou, Beijing-Shanghai, Beijing-Wuhu, and Huainan Railways 173

In recent years, educational authorities in various countries have utilized educational films as auxiliary teaching tools, and their effectiveness has become increasingly apparent. The International Educational Film Association has requested teachers at all levels of schools in various countries to dedicate their time and energy to beneficial efforts in instructional films, organizing "Educational Film Pioneers." Schools in various countries have actively responded. According to experiments conducted by many renowned American professors and companies producing educational films using instructional films, the conclusions reached include: Students using films acquire 19% more knowledge than those not using films; students of average ability using films achieve the same level of learning as high-achieving students without films; teachers of various subjects praise the effectiveness of films; they can enhance creativity and increase participation in design work and self-directed activities; and the benefits of acquiring knowledge difficult to obtain through life experiences using films are countless. The Chinese Educational Film Association, to promote experimental film teaching and enhance the efficiency of film instruction, has specially selected twenty reels each of physics, chemistry, and biology films suitable for middle school students. It plans to send personnel to each school adopting instructional films three times in both spring and autumn semesters, allowing physics students to watch physics films, chemistry students to watch chemistry films, and biology students to watch biology films. Teachers of the respective subjects at each school will provide explanations alongside the films. The promotion area is temporarily limited to public and private middle schools along the Shanghai-Hangzhou, Beijing-Shanghai, Beijing-Wuhu, and Huainan railways, with gradual expansion planned for the future. The fees for each period are quite reasonable and can be paid in installments. The association has sent letters to schools along the four railways to discuss this matter and has also requested the educational bureaus of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Beijing, and Shanghai to inform their respective schools about adoption. It is anticipated that this new educational facility will greatly benefit school education. The association's promotion guidelines and film list are provided below.

Promotion Guidelines: Chinese Educational Film Association Promotion Guidelines for Instructional Films. To promote instructional films and experiment with film education, the association will temporarily select twenty reels each of physics, chemistry, and biology films suitable for middle school students, and conduct traveling screenings. For each instructional film mentioned above, the association will pre-print instruction manuals. The promotion area is temporarily limited to middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools along the Shanghai-Hangzhou, Beijing-Shanghai, Beijing-Wuhu, and Huainan railways. Each semester, the association will send personnel to each school for three screenings, with each screening showing two or four reels of physics, chemistry, and biology films (lasting approximately sixty minutes) for students to view. For each subject's instructional films, the teachers of that subject at each school will refer to the instruction manual to create their own teaching plans and provide detailed explanations during the screenings. Each school may participate in any one, two, or all three subjects. The fee standards are as follows: (1) Participating in one subject costs 30 yuan per semester; (2) two subjects cost 50 yuan; (3) three subjects cost 60 yuan. The aforementioned fees may be paid in installments or in one lump sum. Each school must provide black cloth curtains to block sunlight for the screening venue. The association will provide the screen, projector, and other equipment. The association will pre-arrange the screening schedule for each school and notify them one week in advance, along with the instruction manual. Schools must not make any changes to avoid delaying screenings at other schools. The schools are not obligated to provide meals and accommodation for the association's projectionist, but in special circumstances, they may be requested to assist.

Film Titles: Physics, Spring Semester, First Term: Magnetic Effects of Electricity, Chemical Effects of Electricity, The Story of Edison; Second Term: Solar Energy, Light and Heat from Electricity, Steam Engine; Third Term: Light of Mankind, Lenses, Uses of Lamps, Radio. Autumn Semester, First Term: Simple Machines, Tap Water, Atmospheric Pressure; Second Term: High-Pressure Air, Hydraulic Power, Pneumatic Power; Third Term: Water Cycle, Ice Making, Internal Combustion Engine, Weather Forecasting. Tai Shuangqiu Performs Yesterday: Popular Education Cart. Reports on Invention Process and Function. Ministry of Education Orders Nationwide Adoption. 174

Dr. Tai Shuangqiu, Doctor of Education from Columbia University and current Dean of the School of Education at Great China University in Shanghai, has been engaged in rural education for years, advocating for people's livelihood-based education, which has attracted considerable attention from the national education community. Dr. Tai, recognizing that current education is costly and its content is biased towards imparting literacy, serving as a decoration for a small number of elite classes, making it difficult to effectively popularize among the general public, invented a "Popular Education Cart" after years of experimentation to address this issue. This invention was previously publicly demonstrated by Dr. Tai in Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, and other provinces, earning praise from the education community. Recently, the Ministry of Education reviewed and deemed it ingeniously constructed, easy to carry, and a valuable tool for promoting compulsory education and popular education. It has ordered compulsory education and popular education institutions nationwide to adopt it. Mr. Tai hosted a reception for newspaper reporters at Yizhixiang last night at 7 PM, first explaining the function and structure of the Popular Education Cart for popularizing education, and then holding a demonstration. All attendees praised it, and the event concluded at 9:30 PM. The structure, function, and features of the cart are described separately below. Photo of Tai Shuangqiu and his invented Popular Education Cart (International Press Photo).

Structure: The Popular Education Cart's external appearance is a rectangular wooden box, about one meter long, thirty centimeters wide, and seventy centimeters high. It has three wheels at the bottom, one large wheel in front and two small wheels in the back, allowing it to be pushed to various locations. The front and back panels of the cart can be flipped up to serve as a blackboard, and when laid flat, they become a table one meter wide and two meters long, suitable for displays, exhibitions, ping pong, and various activities. There are two types of iron frames on the cart, usually stored inside the cart, and when used, they can be taken out to form a canopy frame for hanging blackboards, charts, oil lamps, books, abacuses, and other items. A cloth curtain can also be attached to the cart. The cart frame and edges have measuring scales for body and fabric measurements. Inside the cart, there are six versatile Popular Education Boxes, storing various supplies for health education, entertainment, crafts, and agricultural product exhibitions. When needed, one box can be selected based on the occasion and carried on the back, without hindering travel over mountains and streams. The cart also has four folding educational stools, two of which combine to form the cart's top cover, while the other two are stored inside the cart, taking up very little space when folded and providing seating for eight people when unfolded, with sturdy connections to prevent tipping.

Function: The Popular Education Cart has an ingenious structure and can fully utilize all its parts. Its main uses include a traveling library, mobile lecture hall, popular newspaper office, mobile exhibition hall, substitute meeting place, commoner's desk, temporary hospital, cooperative store, simple workshop, agricultural guidance, entertainment venue, and open-air tea garden, covering all aspects of education, including literacy, civics, health, livelihood, and leisure.

Features: The cart's features can be summarized in four words: affordable and versatile. The cart has all the above functions, which ordinary educational institutions, such as schools and popular education centers, cannot provide. Even if they could, they would require large buildings, extensive equipment, and numerous personnel, costing thousands of dollars. The value of the Popular Education Cart, including the cart body, frame, educational stools, educational boxes, and over two hundred pieces of equipment and supplies for literacy, health, leisure, cooperation, civics, and livelihood education, totals only eighty-some yuan. The administrator requires only one person, making the cost savings evident. This is its first feature. Popular education institutions have fixed locations, and only a small number of people benefit from them. However, many people lack educational opportunities due to their professions, inconvenient transportation, or traditional ideas. The education efficiency is reduced as a result. Now, the education cart can be pushed to various places, from mountaintops to watersides, to remote villages, reaching all places. It travels to various locations throughout the day and provides education in rotation. One cart can reach hundreds of people, and the equipment can be fully utilized without waste. This is its second feature. Combining these two points, the greatness of the education cart and the economy of its cost can be seen.

Scope of Application: The application of the Popular Education Cart is extensive. Generally speaking, it has the following uses: Education bureaus and education departments of various counties can use the cart to popularize compulsory education. It meets the requirements of the Ministry of Education's outline for implementing compulsory education, and mobile education cannot be carried out without using the cart. Local popular education centers, farmer education centers, libraries, etc., can use the cart to divide into several mobile education centers or mobile libraries to promote extramural popular education. Local popular schools can use the cart to divide into several mobile popular schools to increase the efficiency of popular education. Local elementary and middle schools can use the cart to assist extracurricular volunteer education and popular education to train students' ability to serve society. Local teachers should use the cart as the central hub, guiding young teachers to use the various educational boxes inside the cart to assist in the popularization of education. Education colleges and departments, normal schools, and secondary school normal departments in various universities should offer "Mobile Education" courses and use the cart to train students. Other educational institutions and organizations should use the cart to assist in volunteer education.

It is heard that Mr. Tai, to meet the needs of the education community, has entrusted the Education Compilation and Translation Center at 750 Jessfield Road, Shanghai, to manufacture and distribute the cart. Pre-orders are currently being accepted, with the full set of equipment and supplies, totaling over two hundred pieces, priced at only eighty-five yuan for pre-orders. The deadline is March 15, extended to the end of March for remote provinces. The center also has detailed brochures available for request.

Photo of Tai Shuangqiu and his invented Popular Education Cart (International Press Photo).

The association will arrange the performance time and date for registered children according to their age and send them to them in advance. Those with excellent results will be given prizes and requested the National Children's Year Implementation Committee to commend. The performance results are the property of the association. The association will provide all the utensils needed during the performance. Matters not covered may be amended by the meeting at any time.

Since the Shanghai branch of the Alumni Association of graduates from National Nankou, Dongda, and Zhongda Universities took over Guohua Middle School on Gordon Road in this city, the school has been completely renovated, and both teachers and students are very motivated. Every Monday, a memorial week is held, and learned and well-known people are invited to give lectures. Yesterday (the 2nd), the school invited Ren Mengxian, a pioneer in Jiangsu education, former principal of the Jiangsu Provincial Fifth Normal School for more than ten years, and current professor at Great China University, to give a lecture on education in extraordinary times during the memorial week. Principal Tian Dingan first introduced him, and then Mr. Ren elaborated on the various aspects that should be emphasized and implemented in education during extraordinary times. The most important aspects are spiritual training and physical training. Spiritual training should be based on developing national consciousness and observing discipline. After the lecture, Principal Tian gave a thank-you speech and reported on the international situation. After the ceremony, over three hundred teachers and students were very excited and applauded to thank Mr. Ren for his enthusiastic guidance.

Shi Chongpeng's "Notes on Appreciating Famous Chinese Paintings" 180

Renowned painter Shi Chongpeng recently based his "Notes on Appreciating Famous Chinese Paintings" on the famous paintings in the London Chinese Art Exhibition. The content is rich, including over one hundred famous painters from the Tang, Five Dynasties, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties, and over two hundred famous paintings. The composition, brushwork, inscriptions, poems, and colophons are all recorded and described in detail. The residences, official positions, and ancestral origins of each famous painter are also studied in detail. The authenticity and quality are evaluated appropriately, and the identification is accurate. It also includes thirty film strips of fine, ethereal, and wondrous works from past dynasties, which are rarely seen in historical records, making it a remarkable work. It is undoubtedly an outstanding work that helps in the appreciation of famous paintings and the verification of painting history. The beginning of the compilation is signed by contemporary senior painter Xiao Wuquan, and prefaces are written by renowned scholars Wang Qingmu and renowned painters He Tianjian and Zheng Wuchang. The entire book contains over 50,000 words and more than thirty illustrations. The combination of text and images makes it a valuable resource for everyone. It will be published by the Commercial Press soon.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (188) 181

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"That is really the best, funniest thing I ever saw, especially those fellows," said Mr. Rice, jumping out of the room, for they had let him into the secret, and now he went along laughing like a great boy, now it was all over.

"Here they come; I heard Emil call out, 'Down with the landlubbers,' so we must hurry and dress," cried Nan, and away they all scampered upstairs.

The boys came back like a troop of lions; their breath of air had given them appetites that would have made a turkey tremble if that fowl had possessed the power of fear. Away they went to dress; and in half an hour such a scrubbing, brushing, and furbishing was going on, that any tidy woman would have been glad to see it. When the bell rang, a troop of rosy-faced boys, with shining heads, white collars, and Sunday clothes, filed into the dining-room, where Mrs. Jo, in her one black silk, with a beloved white rose at her throat, sat at the head of the long table, and, as the boys said, looked "stately and beautiful," as they always thought she did when she was in full dress. Miss May and Nan had on their new winter frocks, with bright sashes and bows, and looked as gay as flower-beds. Tommy, in his scarlet knitted suit and beaded boots, was also brilliant in his way.

Mr. and Mrs. Bhaer glanced at each other at the foot of the long table, and then at the row of happy faces on each side, and felt that they too had something to be grateful for, but there was no need to say a word, for one heart said to the other: "Our work is prospering, we must be thankful, and try again."
